  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c6c23a9f-c07b-4f8a-aacf-8f48e0adb107'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

After a very difficult recovery, she’s been uprooted across the country and forced into the custody of a father that abandoned her when she was a young child. If Ella wants to escape her father’s home and her awful new stepfamily, she must convince her doctors that she’s capable, both physically and emotionally, of living on her own. The problem is, she’s not ready yet. The only way she can think of to start healing is by reconnecting with the one person left in the world who’s ever meant anything to her—her anonymous Internet best friend, Cinder. <br />… <br />Hollywood sensation Brian Oliver has a reputation for being trouble. There’s major buzz around his performance in his upcoming film The Druid Prince, but his management team says he won’t make the transition from teen heartthrob to serious A-list actor unless he can prove he’s left his wild days behind and become a mature adult. In order to douse the flames on Brian’s bad-boy reputation, his management stages a fake engagement for him to his co-star Kaylee. Brian isn’t thrilled with the arrangement—or his fake fiancée—but decides he’ll suffer through it if it means he’ll get an Oscar nomination. Then a surprise email from an old Internet friend changes everything.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2324459667" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4164040600693442942">THIS WAS THE CONTEMPORARY ROMANCE I NEEDED. It was so cute (and so cheesy in a good way). I loved it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1147942894" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1147942894" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1147942894?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/34117027-olivia-savannah-roach">Olivia-Savannah  Roach</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=celebrity">celebrity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=cheesy">cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=unrealistic">unrealistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=cinderella">cinderella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147942894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15460685774630309508"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420009556ra/13153984.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>2.5 stars.</b> This turned out to be the kind of book that was agreeable enough to read (the first 50% more than the other half though) but that, when you think of the content, right after finishing it, it may possibly be that you end up having very mixed thoughts. That’s how I feel. I enjoyed reading it and getting to know the characters – some of them – but I nonetheless cannot stop thinking about how improbable it was for this story to actually take place in our world. Well, I know it is fiction </span>
  <span id="freeText15460685774630309508" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420009556ra/13153984.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>2.5 stars.</b> This turned out to be the kind of book that was agreeable enough to read (the first 50% more than the other half though) but that, when you think of the content, right after finishing it, it may possibly be that you end up having very mixed thoughts. That’s how I feel. I enjoyed reading it and getting to know the characters – some of them – but I nonetheless cannot stop thinking about how improbable it was for this story to actually take place in our world. Well, I know it is fiction + contemporary + fairy tale retelling, but there are some books and, hell, movies and retellings of Cinderella that you can come to actually BELIEVE in and imagine happening for REAL. This is not one of them. And that’s a shame, in my opinion, because it could have been the type of story to make you dream!<br><br>It was a light read and not that long. Quite easy to get into too. The author created a main character that we can relate to – well well, she was actually a blogger herself and reviewer of books! – plus a secondary cast very wide and containing a variety of different personalities. That was fun! She really did succeed at making this an entertaining read. But the thing is…It is strange how entertaining it actually ended up being since there were some pretty heavy and important themes in there. Ella’s life wasn’t perfect at all! Her mom died…she thought her father didn’t love her…and her new sister-in-laws acted like terrific creatures (okay, perhaps that was an intended hyperbole). <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420009556ra/13153987.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Cinderella’s life itself wasn’t easy either, but Ella wasn’t feeling good about it all and was weak…yet strong, we could feel it. The author, I assume, tried to make us realize this but the execution was so-so because, like I said, this was a fairy tale! And so melodramatic that it had transformed some emotional scenes into banal ones. Something I thought was not great. Ella suffered, but I didn’t quite feel it. I guess, to sum it up, this could have simply been less focused on Ella’s problems and *depression* (I didn’t feel like she was depressed at all! How her father kept wanting to hospitalize her in fact bothered me!) and more on the actual romance.<br><br>Oh yeah…the romance. That was crazy but Cinder and Ella didn’t actually meet in *real life* before something like 60% of the story (this is an average). It dragged! It may have been fast-paced and full of (unrelated to the romance) events that weren’t necessarily boring, but it did drag since this, as main purpose, was supposed to be a Cinderella retelling! ...Right? At least, that’s all I wanted from it. While we could see some similarities to the classic, there were SO many new elements that were created by the other. For instance, Ella’s new stepmother was in reality really really sweet and caring and so nice with her new daughter-in-law. Which was lovely, but the atmosphere was not the same. Yet, I understand since in the real tale Ella’s father was death while in this book he was alive. No, instead of having a despicable stepmother, we had a wicked little *bitchy* girlfriend. Cinder’s, incidentally. That added some spicy flavour to the plot though.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420009556ra/13153989.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cinder…oh I’m sorry but, sincerely, I never saw you and Ella making that of a perfect and charming couple. I mean, you were cute as a whole, for the most part, but definitely better off as best friends. Like you primarily were. For more than half of the book! And there was a love-triangle. A VERY unnecessary and unpleasant love-triangle. I swear, there were so many characters in this book. Which wasn’t a bad thing itself, it’s the consequences that they may have had on the story that bothered me. Rob, for example, confused Ella’s heart for nothing! <br><br>Not bad, but not great either. This felt like a mix between the movie <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0356470/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Cinderella Story</a> and <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1071358/" rel="nofollow noopener">Another Cinderella Story</a> so, I guess, if you enjoyed both of those films, you might very likely find yourself spending some lovely hours with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22724488.Cinder___Ella" title="Cinder &amp; Ella by Kelly Oram" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder &amp; Ella</a>!<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15460685774630309508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I loved it! <b>I EFFING LOVED IT! </b>That <b>goofy smile</b> on my face is just the tip of the iceberg! I can feel my heart dancing salsa and pink clouds raining candy canes on my head! I need a moment to thank <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8440277.Rachel_E__Carter' title='Rachel E. Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel E. Carter</a> for recommending me this book. Seriously Rachel, you're like the cute contemporary guru!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448885188ra/17202537.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22724488.Cinder___Ella' title='Cinder & Ella by Kelly Oram' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cinder & Ella</a> is a (surprise,</span>
  <span id="freeText16639926376108181783" style="display:none">Richard and Kahlan.<br>She mentioned <i>Richard and Kahlan</i>.<br>Ella almost fainted when she got to meet <i>
  <b>Richard and Kahlan.</b>
</i><br>Excuse me while I try to compose myself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467395118ra/19588306.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved it! I loved it! <b>I EFFING LOVED IT! </b>That <b>goofy smile</b> on my face is just the tip of the iceberg! I can feel my heart dancing salsa and pink clouds raining candy canes on my head! I need a moment to thank <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8440277.Rachel_E__Carter" title="Rachel E. Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel E. Carter</a> for recommending me this book. Seriously Rachel, you're like the cute contemporary guru!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448885188ra/17202537.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22724488.Cinder___Ella" title="Cinder &amp; Ella by Kelly Oram" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder &amp; Ella</a> is a (surprise, surprise!) <b>Cinderella retelling</b> taking place in Hollywood. Only the stepmother isn't evil, the father is alive, Prince Charming is a <b>swoonworthy playboy</b> and Cinderella a <b>fantasy geek</b>. The real villain, besides the awful, I-wanna-strangle-you-bitch Kaylee, is the society. The society that can't show compassion to a girl who lost her mother and was damaged both mentally and physically during the accident that turned her world upside down. Being bullied all the time and feeling unwanted by a family she just got to meet, Ella's only sunshine was her internet friend Cinder. She never met him in person, but she felt like she had known him her entire life. And the best part is (the one I absolutely adored) that the reason it all started was their love for the same fantasy books! I <i>love</i> nerdy protagonists! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468508876ra/19715976.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ella's misfortunes often brought me tears, I didn't expect to become so <b>emotional</b> while reading it. And let's just say that I fell in love with Cinder pretty much from the start! He was so cocky and hot and tried to hide his inner nerd that it was inevitable! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3203095.Kelly_Oram" title="Kelly Oram" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly Oram</a> did an amazing job with the rest of the characters as well. I loved Vivian and Rob and Juliette and Jessica, I even understood Ana's attitude (which is very hard to admit). While the story wasn't complex (I dare say it was <b>predictable</b>) I loved every single thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22724488.Cinder___Ella" title="Cinder &amp; Ella by Kelly Oram" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder &amp; Ella</a>, especially the interactions and the dialogues between them, they cracked me up and made me wanna die due to <b>overwhelming feelings</b> and squeal and speak gibberish and <b>fangirl</b> in every possible way!! I know for sure that I'm going to read more from Kelly Oram because she won a place in my heart!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468508876ra/19715977.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

I loved this book. I loved everything about it. Yes, it may not be the most original, the most literary, the most developed, etc., etc. but it made me smile the whole time I was reading it. This book was just a really sweet romance and I didn't even mind the switching POV'S (!!!) -which is huuuge because I never like them.<br/><br/>Kelly Oram reminds me of Meg Cabot in her writing style -that fuzzy, feel good, fast-paced awesomeness that I fell in love with in middle school.   <span id="freeText11485919318896071708" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419272167ra/13024967.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AWWWWW. This book was just a really sweet romance and I didn't even mind the switching POV'S (!!!) -which is huuuge because I never like them.<br><br>Kelly Oram reminds me of Meg Cabot in her writing style -that fuzzy, feel good, fast-paced awesomeness that I fell in love with in middle school. This is the book you read when you are in the mood for something light between big fantasy/dystopia books. This book is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Ella Enchanted by Gail Carson Levine" rel="nofollow noopener">Ella Enchanted</a> in YA contemporary the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11235712.Cinder__The_Lunar_Chronicles___1_" title="Cinder (The Lunar Chronicles, #1) by Marissa Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinder</a> is it for sci-fi.<br><br>I can't wait to read more by Kelly!</span>

<div id="review_1076390033" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1076390033" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1076390033?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Someone Who Doesn't Get Bogged Down by Lack of Research</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nasty Lady MJ by: </span>
      Kindle
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=cringe-worthy-covers">cringe-worthy-covers</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=just-not-my-thing">just-not-my-thing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=offensive">offensive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=it-had-so-much-potential-but">it-had-so-much-potential-but</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=diversity">diversity</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1076390033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16960095082930122541">To see review with gifs click <a href='http://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/10/11/and-this-is-why-no-one-likes-lawyerscinder-and-ella-by-kelly-oram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>You know what I hate about being a lawyer, the fact that I can’t watch Law and Order or any other lawyer-ish show and call foul anytime something isn’t factually correct. The thing is, I give the shows a lot of leeway. For the most part, they actually try to do research about the legal issues they’re presenting.<br/><br/>I don’t think Kelly Oram did that all with Cinder and Ella or she probably didn’t care. But it really annoys me.<br/><br/>Before I go into particulars, I am going</span>
  <span id="freeText16960095082930122541" style="display:none">To see review with gifs click <a href="http://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/10/11/and-this-is-why-no-one-likes-lawyerscinder-and-ella-by-kelly-oram/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />You know what I hate about being a lawyer, the fact that I can’t watch Law and Order or any other lawyer-ish show and call foul anytime something isn’t factually correct. The thing is, I give the shows a lot of leeway. For the most part, they actually try to do research about the legal issues they’re presenting.<br /><br />I don’t think Kelly Oram did that all with Cinder and Ella or she probably didn’t care. But it really annoys me.<br /><br />Before I go into particulars, I am going to give a bit of a disclaimer. Going into this I was sort of weary. My first appearance with Oram was DNF-ville with that terrible superhero book of hers where parents pushed their daughter to be with an annoying stalker. Everyone was awful in that book.<br /><br />It shouldn’t surprise me then, that everyone was an asshole in Cinder and Ella as well.<br /><br />Strike two against the book.<br /><br />And what about strike three? I already mentioned the legal and factual inaccurcies, the horrible characters, oh and did I mention unnecessary melodrama that relates back to items two and three.<br /><br />Sigh…<br /><br />Do I have anything nice to say before I get my Book Hulk on? Well, Oram tried with this one. I liked the fact we had a diverse character, who was prickly, and who wasn’t stereotypically pretty. But everything sort of fell apart that aside.<br /><br />Sigh…<br /><br />For the rest of the review I’m going to divide it into three categories: 1) Legal/Factual Issues, 2) Assholes, and 3) Melodrama. I think by doing this I can sort of sort out my feelings without having my head explode and make sense of what’s going to be some rather rambily rants. Because guys, this book kept me up all last night because I was raging.<br /><br />1) Legal/Factual Issues: In Other Words Orum Contributes to a Lawyer’s Bad Mood<br /><br />I think this will be a me category more than the other categories on here, but it really annoys me when non-lawyer authors don’t even do the barest amount of research one legal issues like getting someone declared freaking incompetent.<br /><br />Or about the American Disabilities Act.<br /><br />A couple of Google searches would’ve told them all they needed to know.<br /><br />Yes, I said Google. Because while she needed to do some research, it isn’t like she needs to read case law, but if you just Google celebrities who were declared incompetent you’ll find that it’s a difficult thing to do. Having one suicide attempt way back in the past probably isn’t going to be enough, especially if the character doesn’t try to harm themselves since and has fairly rationale goals and views on life-i.e. she just wants to go to college. However, apparently not figuring out the exact dormitory you’re going to live in equals unstable according to her not so wonderful shrink.<br /><br />Just like with declaring someone incompetent, it’s extremely difficult to have someone committed. You’re only going to be committed, generally speaking when you’re an imminent threat to yourself or others and that did not happen here. Yet, the main character is constantly threatened by her own shrink about going to a mental institute all because she doesn’t want to be a super extrovert and make friends.<br /><br />Because heaven forbid someone likes to have alone time and reading a fucking book.<br /><br />That equals unstable you know. I’ll tell you what’s unstable me after reading this book.<br /><br />I should mention said shrink threatened her after a traumatizing event that was no way her own fault.<br /><br />Yes, I’d be a little depressed after someone fucking tore a skin graft and treated me like a monster in home room too. I probably wouldn’t want to go to prom either.<br /><br />I guess I”m sort of overlapping into areas two and three now.<br /><br />But I just want to say if that was my shrink I’d call her an asshole then ask for a second opinion before reporting her to the freaking ethics committees.<br /><br />Now, I’m not a shrink, but threatening a patient like that doesn’t ring like good idea to me. Especially when said patient just experienced trauma. And you’re yelling at them because they didn’t join the pom squad.<br /><br />Fuck you.<br /><br />Then there’s the whole part about how the character should be sent to a special school just because she has a limp and some scarring.<br /><br />Really?<br /><br />Fucking really?<br /><br />Ever heard of the ADA, Oram? I’m even linking it here because I found this part just appalling. And she has scars. So freaking what. This is the twenty-first century most of us who have a some sense of compassion and maturity do not make fun of a person because they have a physical disability. Sure, there are some assholes out there, but the majority of people aren’t like that. Or if they are they aren’t so openly cruel about it.<br /><br />Seriously, you think a school administrator already threatened by a litigious lawyer parent would not even open his asshole mouth about that.<br /><br />But since they’re all asshole (which is an obvious hook to point number too) well….<br /><br />2) Assholes: Because Everyone in this Book was a Cast Member of Spaceballs<br /><br />Yes, they’re all assholes even are lead who I feel sympathy for. But she’s still an asshole too.<br /><br />Though she has a reason to be an asshole unlike everyone else.<br /><br />To be honest, it just felt unrealistic. And reminded me why I didn’t like the Jaime Baker series because Oram can’t create character that have a shred of decency or that aren’t borderline creepy for the life of her.<br /><br />Okay, maybe the nurses and doctors who were bit roles acted like normal people, but that was probably because I didn’t know them.<br /><br />Everyone. And I mean, everyone was douche like in this book. And unsympathetic. Don’t believe me let’s go down the list:<br /><br />Ella: Has a chip on her shoulder, though it’s understandable. But sometimes I just wanted to shake her.<br /><br />Brian: Ha! Ha! Ha! Weak, weak, weak. No backbone there. Seriously, allowing himself to be blackmailed like that (shudders). Makes him a stupid asshole.<br /><br />Ella’s Father: Dick. Who doesn’t even try to listen to his daughter. And doesn’t even consult her before he cleans out her dead mother’s apartment. And if my father threw out my books….well….<br /><br />Stepmom: Bitch who actually tells stepdaughter how bad she looks and suggests plastic surgery and doesn’t understand how that upsets her.<br /><br />Stepsister 1: Well, no one would be surprised that her mother is Lilith (see above).<br /><br />Stepsister 2: Spineless<br /><br />Stepsister’s Boytoy: Evil incarnate<br /><br />Psychiatrist: Sadistic quack. Who needs to have license revoked ASAP.<br /><br />Principal: A lawyer’s worst nightmare who lacks any sort of sensitivity.<br /><br />Ella’s Dead Mother: A personification of offensive culture cliches.<br /><br />Do I need to be continue?<br /><br />To be fair, some characters, like the dead mother, personalities weren’t the cause of their a-holeness. It’s not their thought they’re depicted in such a 1D way. But as for Ella’s family and quack of a shrink.<br /><br />They can all stuff it.<br /><br />3) Melodrama: Duh, they’re Teenagers<br /><br />The melodrama in this one was overdone and obviously unrealistic. However, unlike some books where I can just deal with it. I couldn’t here. So many of the situations could’ve been avoided. Don’t believe me, I’m going to play let’s solve everyone’s problem in a short paragraph or less:<br /><br />1) Ella being forced with her dad because she’s declared incompetent and now has to please him and that quack of a shrink:<br /><br />Answer: Get a new shrink and find an attorney that can represent you. Yes, expensive. But there are ways to work around it (aka legal aid). Grant it, you’re not going to probably get the best of the best, but it still could work given the situation. Plus, if you have access to funds after you’re declared competent problem solved. Or if you had access to funds before being declared incompetent (which I’m assuming you did) you could’ve been declared competent that way. Honestly, based on the sketchy details that we had I had a hard time buying this situation.<br /><br />2) Ella’s father saying how she’s not social:<br /><br />Answer: Treat her like a human being and tell your stepdaughters and wife to act like a decent human being. Also, realize that she’s probably not going to like you because you skipped out on like more than half of her life.<br /><br />3) Brian being forced to be engaged with Kaylee because she’s blackmailing him.<br /><br />Answer: Call Perez Hilton or TMZ and expose her. Trust me, if you’re that big of a teen idol you’ll still get roles. Hollywood is always looking for a good sob story and to villainize someone. Problem solved.<br /><br />4) Someone treating you like a dick in school.<br /><br />Answer: Confront them. And press charges when they rip your skin graft. I’m sorry, but I had no sympathy for that asshole and did not like or approve how the main character was willing to give him a break because he was young. He assaulted her. She might need surgery. It was uncalled for, and I HATE it when the author has the character be like I’ll give him a second chance. No. No. No. No. No.<br /><br />5) When a school suggests you might be better off with your “own kind” (other people with disabilities).<br /><br />Answer: Threaten to lawyer up and sue the bastards. Or at least get the media on their asses. Once again, they’d totally back your back because sob story.<br /><br />I DNF’d pretty much after that when it was suggested that the main character go to a mental institute because she wasn’t joining any extracurricular and being social.<br /><br />Rolls eyes.<br /><br />I’m sorry, not joining after school basket weaving does not mean you need to be institutionalized. This book just put me in so much rage that I couldn’t sleep the night after I read it. It was actually an interesting idea. I looked forward to getting in some gooey sappy cheese with a heroine who had disabilities. You know, if done right it could’ve been good. If Oram was so insistent about giving the father control of everything, she should’ve just kept the main character seventeen. It would’ve been easier and annoyed me less. And I really wish I could get a fictional character’s therapist license revoked because that shrink….<br /><br />Overall Rating: DNF. But even though I despised you book, at least you gave me an emotional and memorable reaction. That’s something, right?</span>
  <a data-text-id="16960095082930122541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1470412038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1470412038" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1470412038?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23203752-cinder-ella">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Inge by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter">Rachel E. Carter</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=wishlist-paperback">wishlist-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=1to-reread">1to-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470412038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3375925536754429508"><b>4.5 stars </b><br/><br/><i>Cinder & Ella</i> is without a doubt one of the most beautiful and sad books I’ve ever had the pleasure of reading. Even going in with different expectations, I did not get disappointed. While I was expecting a light and fluffy read, instead I got a dose of all the feels. Which was fine, because this book was amazing.<br/><br/>Cinder and Ella both lead hectic lives in their own way, and they each find solace and peace in the same thing: a chatroom where they can talk for hours on end. They are, esse</span>
  <span id="freeText3375925536754429508" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars </b><br /><br /><i>Cinder &amp; Ella</i> is without a doubt one of the most beautiful and sad books I’ve ever had the pleasure of reading. Even going in with different expectations, I did not get disappointed. While I was expecting a light and fluffy read, instead I got a dose of all the feels. Which was fine, because this book was amazing.<br /><br />Cinder and Ella both lead hectic lives in their own way, and they each find solace and peace in the same thing: a chatroom where they can talk for hours on end. They are, essentially, best friends, and know pretty much everything about each other except for their first names. However, there are a few secrets left.<br />What he doesn’t know is that Ella was in a gruesome car accident, lost her mother, spent eight months in rehab, and is now for 70% covered in burn marks.<br />What she doesn’t know is that Cinder is actually Brian Oliver, Hollywood’s next teenage heartthrob, <i>and</i> about to play the lead role in <i>The Cinder Chronicles</i>, a movie adaptation of their favourite book series.<br /><br />At times, I felt like Ella’s story was going to tear my heart in two. The way she would get either ignored or bullied at school for not looking like everyone else, the way she never truly fit in with her new family, how her body would never be her own anymore. It was absolutely heart-breaking to watch her going through the motions of what others have taken for granted. She walks with a cane, she can’t fully stretch her right (mangled) hand, she was forced to move in with a father who left her when she was 8 years old. At times, it was really difficult to read. I don’t usually cry when I’m reading something, but this time I did have something in my eye a few times.<br /><br />The only one she can truly count on is Cinder, and even so, he’s in a bit of a pickle of his own. His life is being dictated to him and he doesn’t have any input – up to the point where they decide who he gets engaged to. Their lives are turned upside down when they meet by happenstance at a fantasy convention, but there are so many complications that can’t be ignored.<br /><br /><i>Cinder &amp; Ella</i> wasn’t without fault and did have a handful of clichés, but the high rating is because of the fact that I couldn’t put it down and read the entire thing within 24 hours. It is because it made me <i>feel</i> so many things, because I truly sympathised with Ella, because I loved Ella and wanted to hug her and tell her everything would be alright. It is because I would recommend this book to anyone who’s a contemporary fan, because it was cute and swoon-worthy and definitely a new favourite.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3375925536754429508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1136882568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1136882568" />
    <a title="Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9871824-ash"><img alt="Ash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600418979p2/9871824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1136882568?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash" href="/user/show/9871824-ash">Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9871824-ash?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1136882568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4670927887386068236"><i>first read: April 2 - 3, 2015<br/>first reread: June 20, 2015<br/>second reread: April 3, 2016<br/>third reread: Febryary 1 - ?, 2017</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“You want to know why you’ve never been able to make me cry? Because you’re trying to tear down someone who’s already hit rock bottom. You can’t make me feel any worse about myself than I already do.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>JUNE 2015</b> I was without internet/phone for over 24 hours, so I thought I'd reread some of those 2015 favorites so I wouldn't be upset that I couldn't update on GR.<br/><br/><i>So, of course, </i></span>
  <span id="freeText4670927887386068236" style="display:none"><i>first read: April 2 - 3, 2015<br />first reread: June 20, 2015<br />second reread: April 3, 2016<br />third reread: Febryary 1 - ?, 2017</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“You want to know why you’ve never been able to make me cry? Because you’re trying to tear down someone who’s already hit rock bottom. You can’t make me feel any worse about myself than I already do.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>JUNE 2015</b> I was without internet/phone for over 24 hours, so I thought I'd reread some of those 2015 favorites so I wouldn't be upset that I couldn't update on GR.<br /><br /><i>So, of course, I reread this :)</i><br /><br />I love this story! nothing much has changed from my previous review. I laughed at the same parts, and I am pretty sure I cried at the same parts as well. I didn't love this any less than I did the first time. This is a book I can see myself rereading time and time again.<br /><br />--------<br /><br /><b>APRIL 2015</b><s><i>this is my 80th book read this year....and I wish it had been one of the first. </i><br /><br />This was such an adorable, heartwarming <i>[at times]</i>, devastating <i>[a lot...]</i>, beautiful, gut wrenching, and amazingly wonderful book.<br /><br /><b>I laughed, I cried.....I laughed until I cried....I just...cried....and I smiled....</b> you would think this is 'just' another retelling of Cinderella, <i> but, its so much more than that. </i><br /><br /><u>It's about a girl</u>, who has survived a horrible accident and how she tries to deal with her life as it is now, which is <i>so</i> much different than what she grew up knowing. She is in a new place, with a new family, shes bullied....shes hated....but she is just so strong, and I love her to pieces. <br /><br /><u>It's about a boy</u>, who is so much more under the surface....<br /><br /><b>its about a beautiful friendship <i>that just might be something else entirely.</i></b><br /><br />I loved this book!</s></span>
  <a data-text-id="4670927887386068236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Bonnie Shores" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25177308-bonnie-shores"><img alt="Bonnie Shores" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500403398p2/25177308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2548391441?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie Shores" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie Shores" href="/user/show/25177308-bonnie-shores">Bonnie Shores</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25177308-bonnie-shores?shelf=teen-life">teen-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25177308-bonnie-shores?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25177308-bonnie-shores?shelf=must-re-read">must-re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548391441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16688583714637556678">There is no way I can convey how much this book made me smile.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538417262ra/26384330.gif' width='600' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I was pretty much hooked from the first page. The author did an amazing job of transforming the classic fairy tale into something believable and relatable. An only child of a divorced mom, Ella's life was happy. Until a car accident changed everything. Now forced to live with a dad she doesn't know, a perfect stepmother and her two "mean girl" stepsisters, Ella's life is anything but happy. She's trying hard to adapt to her new circum</span>
  <span id="freeText16688583714637556678" style="display:none">There is no way I can convey how much this book made me smile.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538417262ra/26384330.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was pretty much hooked from the first page. The author did an amazing job of transforming the classic fairy tale into something believable and relatable. An only child of a divorced mom, Ella's life was happy. Until a car accident changed everything. Now forced to live with a dad she doesn't know, a perfect stepmother and her two "mean girl" stepsisters, Ella's life is anything but happy. She's trying hard to adapt to her new circumstances, but just can't seem to fit in with her new family.<br><br>The only thing she has from her past is her blog and Cinder, her online best friend, but she hasn't checked on either of them since her accident more than eight months ago. When she finally emails Cinder, she's ecstatic to discover that he's missed her, and they resume their relationship right where they left off. Neither one knows the real world identity of the other and that's worked for them during their three years of friendship. But Ella's absence forced Cinder to admit his feelings for her, even if it's only to himself. However, he's in an impossible situation where he has very little control over his own life. When an opportunity to meet arises and Cinder declines, Ella is hurt. She's had a secret crush on him for years and always hoped he'd feel the same way some day.<br><br>I don't want to say any more. While a lot of what happens in the story is kind of predictable (it is, after all, a re-telling), it doesn't lessen the impact. There are so many awwwww moments and even a few happy tears. I'll let you discover those moments for yourself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462976136ra/19067559.gif" width="600" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As far as sweet and innocent and non-world-changing goes, this book is now on my all-time favorite list. There wasn't just a happy ending, it was the happiest of endings, just like in a Hallmark movie. 😍❤️<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538417262ra/26384331.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16688583714637556678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13357737170582106824" style="display:none">This book packs a punch. A real punch. I love it! This is my first book by Miss Oram. Will not be my last. <br />I love love Ella.               <span id="reviewTextContainer1462230617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14262379043378544960"><b>*4.25 HAPPILY-EVER-AFTER STARS*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“True beauty comes from inside a person. If you feel beautiful, then you’ll look beautiful to others no matter what’s on the surface.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>This was such a lovely read and just what I needed after the huge mindfuck that is called <i>Dangerous Girls</i> lol.<br/>Make no mistake though, this book dealt with some serious topics like death, bullying, physical and mental scars and so on...<br/><br/><i>Review to come!</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2937503836826490827"><u>First re-read:</u> <br/>Just as amazing as the first time around! It's such a great mash up of real-life and fairy tale - very slightly based on Cinderella. I love that both the main heroine Ella, and Brian, famous movie star are such a fantasy book-lovers! <i>*Ella is also a big fan of Richard and Kahlan!*</i> <br/>They 'met' through her blog, and instantly became best friends for years, until an accident which changed Ella's whole life. Things became much more complicated and their friendship even more essential a</span>
  <span id="freeText2937503836826490827" style="display:none"><u>First re-read:</u> <br />Just as amazing as the first time around! It's such a great mash up of real-life and fairy tale - very slightly based on Cinderella. I love that both the main heroine Ella, and Brian, famous movie star are such a fantasy book-lovers! <i>*Ella is also a big fan of Richard and Kahlan!*</i> <br />They 'met' through her blog, and instantly became best friends for years, until an accident which changed Ella's whole life. Things became much more complicated and their friendship even more essential and indispensable.<br />This book is more meaningful than it may seem by the cover, and it really deserves more hype in my opinion. I, without doubt, recommend to read this book to everyone. It's one of my favourite Contemporaries of all time!<br /><br />☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆☆<br /><br /><br /><u>Original review:</u> <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“A great character needs trials to overcome—experiences to give them depth, to make them vulnerable, relatable, and likable. Good characters need hardships to make them strong. The idea makes sense, but it still sucks if you’re the heroine.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Cinder &amp; Ella</i> is emotionally overwhelming read. This is a story about family, friendship, fame, love, losing beloved person and overcoming terrible accident that turns your life upside down, also about courage and weaknesses. It shows that nothing is only black or white. That every person - even the 'bad one' - has his side of a story. I laughed, I cried, I was enraged and happy at the same time. So don't get fooled by the horrible cover, because <i>Cinder &amp; Ella </i> is definitely worth the read!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Dad was a modern-day Hercules, and it only made his abandonment hurt that much more. I’d always wondered how such a hero, who spent so much time helping others, could be the villain of my story. How could a man like that just walk away, leaving Mama and me on our own?”</i>
</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9299297876566286256">5 stars<br/><br/>A modern twist to an otherwise famous fairytale, this book had me tearing up one second then smiling the next. This is only by first book by Kelly Oram and it was unexpectedly amazing. Not normally a fan of YA, this one made me second guess my reasons for not normally reading YA books. This story had no sex scenes (as expected) however the author made it up with love, family and friendship. This book also deals with abandonment issues and bullying, chapters which really broke my heart. <br/><br/>'C</span>
  <span id="freeText9299297876566286256" style="display:none">5 stars<br /><br />A modern twist to an otherwise famous fairytale, this book had me tearing up one second then smiling the next. This is only by first book by Kelly Oram and it was unexpectedly amazing. Not normally a fan of YA, this one made me second guess my reasons for not normally reading YA books. This story had no sex scenes (as expected) however the author made it up with love, family and friendship. This book also deals with abandonment issues and bullying, chapters which really broke my heart. <br /><br />'Cinder' &amp; Ella meet over the internet and start a beautiful friendship. Unbeknownst to anyone, they are each other's life savers and totally in love. Sadly, a devastating tragedy occurs to Ella and her otherwise happy life flips around. Ella reconnects with Cinder a year later and finds her solace in him.<br />I have never cried for a heroine more than i have for Ella. My gut twisted so hard for the life that was handed to her. The way she felt about her dad and his new family- i was literally.in.tears. WOW! <br /><br />Ella and 'Cinder" have secrets which pretty much make up the rest of the story, but these two characters have the most amazing connection, i could only root for a happy ending. Although it wasn't until the later half of the book,i adored Juliette, Viviane and Rob who made Ella's life so much easier.<br /><br />HIGHLY RECOMMEDED!<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_3007882878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3007882878" />
    <a title="✨ Gramy ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24496452-gramy"><img alt="✨ Gramy ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547080466p2/24496452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3007882878?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ Gramy ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ Gramy ✨ " href="/user/show/24496452-gramy">✨ Gramy ✨ </a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24496452-gramy?shelf=c-romance-contemporary">c-romance-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24496452-gramy?shelf=never-completed">never-completed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24496452-gramy?shelf=c-drama">c-drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3007882878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5395230161960118221">..<br/><b> DESCRIPTION </b><br/><i> It’s been almost a year since eighteen-year-old Ella Rodriguez was in a car accident that left her crippled, scarred, and without a mother. After a very difficult recovery, she’s been uprooted across the country and forced into the custody of a father that abandoned her when she was a young child. If Ella wants to escape her father’s home and her awful new stepfamily, she must convince her doctors that she’s capable, both physically and emotionally, of living on her own. The prob</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5395230161960118221" style="display:none">..<br /><b> DESCRIPTION </b><br /><i> It’s been almost a year since eighteen-year-old Ella Rodriguez was in a car accident that left her crippled, scarred, and without a mother. After a very difficult recovery, she’s been uprooted across the country and forced into the custody of a father that abandoned her when she was a young child. If Ella wants to escape her father’s home and her awful new stepfamily, she must convince her doctors that she’s capable, both physically and emotionally, of living on her own. The problem is, she’s not ready yet. The only way she can think of to start healing is by reconnecting with the one person left in the world who’s ever meant anything to her—her anonymous Internet best friend, Cinder.<br />…<br />Hollywood sensation Brian Oliver has a reputation for being trouble. There’s major buzz around his performance in his upcoming film The Druid Prince, but his management team says he won’t make the transition from teen heartthrob to serious A-list actor unless he can prove he’s left his wild days behind and become a mature adult. In order to douse the flames on Brian’s bad-boy reputation, his management stages a fake engagement for him to his co-star Kaylee. Brian isn’t thrilled with the arrangement—or his fake fiancée—but decides he’ll suffer through it if it means he’ll get an Oscar nomination. Then a surprise email from an old Internet friend changes everything.<br /></i><br /><br />This sounds like an interesting story, but it doesn't warn you about the severity or harshness involved in the experiences that you are willing to allow to impact your mind. Once you absorb these negative scenes, it is most difficult to remove them if you ever can.<br /><br />I listened to the audible version of this story and I was by far more disappointed than I ever expected that I would be. Young adult narratives are usually much more enticing and somewhat uplifting. NOt so with this tale. It aggravated me beyond reason!<br /><br />After losing her mother in a car accident, laying in a coma for a month, and suffering through eight months of tortuous rehab, the heroine is forced to move in with her father and his new family. There was no compassion, no empathy, and no pretense of understanding in her father's house. <br /><br />There was no concern for her feelings or ability to make important personal life choices. This household overflowed with pessimism, overwhelming hostility, and the abominable disdain displayed by the stepmother and her daughters were unconscionable. I can not neglect the totally unnecessary profanity either. <br /><br />Why people choose to force people to fit in places they are not comfortable with doesn't make any sense to me. Sometimes people do understand what is in the best interest of someone else actually is, but sometimes they are so off base that it creates much more damage, causing so much pain and agony that should not be ignored. The icing on the cake was the harsh bullying that no one addressed or corrected - which is totally unacceptable!<br /><br />I pushed through almost seven chapters and then I finally had to give up. Sometimes a book choice is a joy and sometimes it is not. Personally, I felt this was the opposite of joyful. I don't relish having to live through pain and misery, so I exercised my right and chose not to. I know I am in the minority on my opinions of this book, but for me, it was just too disturbing!<br /><br />There are countless books available with the ability to capture my attention without aggravating the crap out of me like this one did. So, off I go . . . <br />..</span>
  <a data-text-id="5395230161960118221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1028816762?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lex" href="/user/show/5559618-lex">Lex</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028816762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3860320907363972911">I'm really a fan of Kelly Oram. :) Just got the ARC! Thank you, Kelly! <3<br/><br/>Days after... Finally finished it! Just now. Lol.<br/><br/>First of all... WHERE CAN I GET THE DRUID CHRONICLES BOOK?!!? <br/><br/>Second, if this is purely fantasy, PLEASE WRITE THE STORY OF DRUID CHRONICLES, KELLY ORAM. I BEG YOU.<br/><br/>Third, I FREAKING LOVE YOU KELLY ORAM. <br/><br/>Fourth, I DEFINITELY LOVE CINDER & ELLA!!! <br/><br/>-REVIEW-<br/><br/>This was such a cheesy story which I definitely enjoyed! All the feels! I have it! Kelly Oram is simply one of the best write</span>
  <span id="freeText3860320907363972911" style="display:none">I'm really a fan of Kelly Oram. :) Just got the ARC! Thank you, Kelly! &lt;3<br /><br />Days after... Finally finished it! Just now. Lol.<br /><br />First of all... WHERE CAN I GET THE DRUID CHRONICLES BOOK?!!? <br /><br />Second, if this is purely fantasy, PLEASE WRITE THE STORY OF DRUID CHRONICLES, KELLY ORAM. I BEG YOU.<br /><br />Third, I FREAKING LOVE YOU KELLY ORAM. <br /><br />Fourth, I DEFINITELY LOVE CINDER &amp; ELLA!!! <br /><br />-REVIEW-<br /><br />This was such a cheesy story which I definitely enjoyed! All the feels! I have it! Kelly Oram is simply one of the best writers. And I am off to preorder the book. Wonder if it'll release a paperback or hardback? Whatever would be available for my collection. :)<br /><br />Some might say the story is cliché, used a lot. I read a lot of novels like this but as always there was the difference. For one, Oram wrote this so cleverly I am in awe of her. She made us laugh, snort, pissed off with some of the characters like Kaylee and all those bullies, be in love with Cinder/Brian and most of all, bawl like a baby with the family drama. <br /><br />I love the family development. I love how it was written out for us to see that they can improve. The can be better. That they have their stories just awaiting to be uncovered. It was not easy reading the family situations like Ella have. With her handicap and issues and scars, I am saluting Ella. Oram shows that Ella is only human, a girl who lost it all but then found out that she still have someone or some people who really care for her. <br /><br />I also like the online relationship part. I can relate. Makes me think that one day, I can definitely meet my online friends. Like meet up with them BEA starts. ;) I'm not closing the possibility it might happen someday. I am looking forward to that day.<br /><br />People might argue with me that the story is just so-so, or whatever. One thing I know, I ENJOYED EVERY SINGLE MINUTE OF READING THIS STORY. I LOVE JULIETTE, VIVIAN AND HER DADS. I LOVE THE FANTASYCON SCENE. AND YOU PEOPLE MUST READ THIS. I can't stress it enough. JUST DO IT, BUY THE BOOK! SPREAD THE WORD, SPREAD THE LOVE OF CINDER &amp; ELLA. &lt;3<br /><br />Kelly Oram is one of my weakness. Lol. I was stressed the whole week but after reading Cinder &amp; Ella, I'm okay. I'm good. <br /><br />Definitely worth reading, worth your time and money. Go to Amazon now! :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="3860320907363972911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4025302624848895141">Reread October 2016<br/><br/>Loved this! <br/><br/>I was not planning on reading this book yet because it doesn't come out until October 1st and there are several other books I really should have read first. I picked up Cinder and Ella to just read the first chapter and didn't put it down! I read the entire thing in one sitting. This really shouldn't have surprised me because I love Kelly Oram! Honestly there are just a few authors that write in a way that sucks me in and won't let me come up for air until I've fin</span>
  <span id="freeText4025302624848895141" style="display:none">Reread October 2016<br /><br />Loved this! <br /><br />I was not planning on reading this book yet because it doesn't come out until October 1st and there are several other books I really should have read first. I picked up Cinder and Ella to just read the first chapter and didn't put it down! I read the entire thing in one sitting. This really shouldn't have surprised me because I love Kelly Oram! Honestly there are just a few authors that write in a way that sucks me in and won't let me come up for air until I've finished their book. Kelly is one of those writers. <br /><br />I'm a sucker for Cinderella retellings so this was destined to be a favorite of mine. What teenage girl hasn't dreamed of having someone famous fall for her and sweep her off her feet. We all know that is not reality but it is sure fun to dream and escape into a fun story like one. <br /><br />Underlying the fairy tale there were beautiful messages about love and acceptance. This book gave me the "feels". I had tears and smiled and laughed out loud. It was a seriously fun escape from the housework that I had intended to do the day I read this.<br /><br />There is some "content" in this one. Nothing as over the top as her book A is for Abstinence contained. I did let my 14 year old read this one but warned her about a few things before she started it and she too loved it.<br /><br />On a random note - I actually googled The Druid Prince a couple chapters into this story because I thought it was a real book and I wanted to read it. Utterly disappointed it isn't a real story... maybe Kelly will write it (hint, hint).<br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars - I loved it.<br /><br />Content: language (I let me teenager read it and she pointed out that there was more than I realized), innuendo and talk of sex but nothing graphic or too over the top.<br /><br />Source: Review copy</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4386752-ezinwanyi-chinyere?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372760721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9568272232859654101">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>This book was all that. It was well written, with great characters. I appreciate that the characters were not ALL good or all bad, they were human with different emotions.<br/><br/>I think I took to Ella immediately because she was a lover of books and a blogger. That made me smile immediately. I could picture her hoarding ARCs and the whole interaction online. It made me think of goodreads.<br/><br/>Ella is so impressive as was Cinder (Brian Oliver). I really empathized wit Ella and what she had been thr</span>
  <span id="freeText9568272232859654101" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />This book was all that. It was well written, with great characters. I appreciate that the characters were not ALL good or all bad, they were human with different emotions.<br /><br />I think I took to Ella immediately because she was a lover of books and a blogger. That made me smile immediately. I could picture her hoarding ARCs and the whole interaction online. It made me think of goodreads.<br /><br />Ella is so impressive as was Cinder (Brian Oliver). I really empathized wit Ella and what she had been through. I was mad at her father for a while, but I saw there was genuine effort to be better. The sisters were trying even though some of the comments were biting. Ella was highly sensitive, understandably so, so I could see where her step sister Juliet and step mother Jennifer were coming from. <br /><br />I couldn't stop listening to this book as I was waiting for Ella to heal emotionally and physically. I wanted her to find that joy of life again. This book was truly a joy because the writing was so visceral and I was just entranced with the story. This is the best cinderella YA retellings I've read. I will definitely check out more work by this author</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/34203782-cinder-ella">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15402332-pam-nelson?shelf=_finished-2018">_finished-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15402332-pam-nelson?shelf=favorite-books-or-series">favorite-books-or-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15402332-pam-nelson?shelf=heavy-issues">heavy-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15402332-pam-nelson?shelf=_finished-2020">_finished-2020</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2397865542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3286518028729959659">5 Star Cinder & Ella<br/><br/>I was looking for something different, and I am so flipping glad I took a chance on this book! <br/><br/>I am not a HUGE fan of YA, because usually there is just too much immature dramalama and it drives me nuts. But I am going to say it... This book had drama yes but in a way that flows with the book.<br/><br/>I was enthralled with Ella, and Cinder and their relationship. I didn’t want to stop listening at any point and I was even sorry when the book ended I wanted more, more, more. <br/><br/>It really i</span>
  <span id="freeText3286518028729959659" style="display:none">5 Star Cinder &amp; Ella<br /><br />I was looking for something different, and I am so flipping glad I took a chance on this book! <br /><br />I am not a HUGE fan of YA, because usually there is just too much immature dramalama and it drives me nuts. But I am going to say it... This book had drama yes but in a way that flows with the book.<br /><br />I was enthralled with Ella, and Cinder and their relationship. I didn’t want to stop listening at any point and I was even sorry when the book ended I wanted more, more, more. <br /><br />It really is a twist on the Cinderella tale but in a completely fresh way. We really get to know the characters well and not just on the surface. This book reminds me of The Sea of Tranquility if anyone has read that YA novel you know what I mean by the depth of a YA book. <br /><br />Ella has a lot of bad going for her but I loved her tenacity, is she broken down? Sure, but she doesn’t make it anyone’s fault when she could. I wouldn’t say she just takes it but she is coping the very best way she knows how. <br />I loved how she asks for help and picks herself up. <br /><br />Cinder was delicious but it was more than that, you fall in love with his heart. His character is just one of those characters you want to keep for yourself. I am calling it he is my BOOK BOYFRIEND... Back off Ladies :p <br /><br />I loved the narration!! I don’t know what a Boston accent is but I would think Kirsten nailed it. Because it wasn’t on every word but it was there. I liked her male voice too... ;) <br /><br />Also really wished this author had more audiobooks because I was going to go get more... :(</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1587215107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1587215107" />
    <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads"><img alt="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380942477p2/4197769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1587215107?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads">Jacqueline&#39;s Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1587215107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1962424825813124858"><b>3 Fairytale stars</b><br/><br/>I’m going against the norm. I wanted a cute, light YA read and yes it had those qualities, it also had a lot of angst and it dragged a bit.<br/><br/>You know the movie, You’ve Got Mail? You know how they didn’t meet until the end of the movie? Well Cinder and Ella is exactly like that. They meet in person a total two times in the book. Had I known that, I am not sure I would have read this book. I kept with the story because I found the storyline adorable and I was just waiting for the tw</span>
  <span id="freeText1962424825813124858" style="display:none"><b>3 Fairytale stars</b><br /><br />I’m going against the norm. I wanted a cute, light YA read and yes it had those qualities, it also had a lot of angst and it dragged a bit.<br /><br />You know the movie, You’ve Got Mail? You know how they didn’t meet until the end of the movie? Well Cinder and Ella is exactly like that. They meet in person a total two times in the book. Had I known that, I am not sure I would have read this book. I kept with the story because I found the storyline adorable and I was just waiting for the two to meet.<br /><br />Cinder and Ella is about two people meeting each other on-line. Ella is a book/movie review, cute I know. Cinder is a mega movie star. Throughout the WHOLE book they converse on-line. I enjoyed reading the conversations they had. It was like I said, cute and adorable.<br /><br />Did I want them to meet in person a lot sooner? Oh yes. <br /><br />Within the first chapter I was hooked into the story. Ella gets in a car accident and loses her mother and is burned over 70% of her body. She now has to live with her father, a father that walked out on her ten years ago. He also has two step daughters.<br /><br />First off, I didn’t like the dad. I tried really hard to understand his reasoning why he would leave his eight year old for another family. This side story was a bit much to read, it was filled with angst and I just didn’t understand why the dad would want to take Ella in even though she is now eighteen. I found that really hard to believe.<br /><br />I really liked the step-sisters. One was mean and one was nice. It added something to the story and I love hating a villain. Ella is teased at school and sometimes it was fine to read and sometimes I question how realistic the situation could be. Are kids that cruel? Sometimes it felt a little too dramatic.<br /><br />Then there’s Ella. She’s a real Debbie downer. She complains throughout the whole book and doesn’t really do anything but close herself off and converse with her on-line friend Cinder, who she doesn’t know is a movie star. At some point I just wanted to slap her and say, yeah, your life sucks, well, do something about it.<br /><br />With all of that said, I think if the main characters meet in real live around the 30% mark and then continued the story from there I would have been a much happier person. Don’t get me wrong, I found the book entertaining, that is why I finished it, but it wasn’t my favorite and it needed major tweaking. <br /><br /><i>READ on KINDLE UNLIMITED</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1962424825813124858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1999880262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3064612472201508413">This book was everything I needed right now. It was deep and sweet and funny. The growing pains and angst felt so real and the banter and witty snark and fandom feels were all just so welcome. It was everything you could want in a a Cinderella retelling that gives you feelings and hope. Every bit of time on this book was well spent, and I'm eager to see what happens to Elle and Brian next.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=awesome-heroes">awesome-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=second-chance">second-chance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=awesome-5-stars-2016-17">awesome-5-stars-2016-17</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=100-book-reading-challenge-2016">100-book-reading-challenge-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=danger-or-hurt">danger-or-hurt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23384676-a-ryan?shelf=fairytale-or-classic-redux">fairytale-or-classic-redux</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1473132030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14705250594646548530">Ignore the cover... this book is AWESOME!!!<br/><br/>I absolutely adored this Cinderella tale... Kelly Oram has managed to put a fresh spin on a story that has been told a thousand times. <br/><br/>I loved Cinder.<br/>I loved Ella.<br/>I loved the friendship between them.<br/>Rob, Juliette, Vivienne (and her two dads) made fantastic fairy godmothers/friendly mice (depending on your interpretation).<br/>I absolutely loved Oram's version of the glass slipper... Didn't see it coming but looking back, I thought it was perfect!<br/><br/>I just loved</span>
  <span id="freeText14705250594646548530" style="display:none">Ignore the cover... this book is AWESOME!!!<br /><br />I absolutely adored this Cinderella tale... Kelly Oram has managed to put a fresh spin on a story that has been told a thousand times. <br /><br />I loved Cinder.<br />I loved Ella.<br />I loved the friendship between them.<br />Rob, Juliette, Vivienne (and her two dads) made fantastic fairy godmothers/friendly mice (depending on your interpretation).<br />I absolutely loved Oram's version of the glass slipper... Didn't see it coming but looking back, I thought it was perfect!<br /><br />I just loved it all!!! It was fun, poignant, heartbreaking and romantic. A thorough delight that will capture the hearts of fans of the modern fairytale genre.<br /><br />This is pure fantasy with some tragic scenes that were pretty tough to read but ultimately it ends with the classic happy ending worthy of both characters and the journey they have travelled. <br /><br />(Note: I'm not sure how realistic the legal aspects of this story were (um, not at all)... so if you're a law student, or a sucker for legal dramas and detailed accuracy, beware the possible dramatic license taken here. My advice would be to just go with it. After all, it's a fairytale).</span>
  <a data-text-id="14705250594646548530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
